unsolicited comment that you'll probably never see Morgan, but I went through a period in my life that was similar to what you seem to be going through, though mine was brought on by trauma and I coped differently than you are, but I can still empathize. I think everyone has to find their path to personal and spiritual development, but... I always tell people that when you're in your twenties, you measure yourself by looking at others, and when you're in your thirties, you measure yourself by the merit of your own accomplishments. so I think growing up will help you, in and of itself, as it did for me. however, in addition to simply maturing, one of the absolute best choices I ever made was to de-vest myself from the opinions of other people and live for myself, all without losing my heart. I also deleted most of my social media, and don't bother with anything but youtube, which is generally less toxic. I really learned to put myself first. I honestly would not change a single thing about who I am as a person, and I am lucky enough to have the willpower and the means to change anything I don't like about my appearance, so what's not to love about myself? I think when you hit rock bottom you learn to fight for yourself, and to be your own best friend. at some point in my life, I got so low, that I somehow had this epiphany. I can't really explain it, but I just became completely sure of myself. it's almost like I hypnotized myself to survive. I honestly believe that I can do anything (within reason) that I put my mind to doing. just honest and true self confidence born from looking the worst possible version of myself dead in the eye, and instead of feeling disgusted, I felt moved to tears by how human I was. I really loved myself at that moment, and I felt beautiful in a strange way. I decided to completely abandoned faith in others, and in the world, which had always let me down, and put all my faith in myself and God/the universe. I think that this change really helped me overcome many of the challenges I was having in my life. although I still seek to improve myself everyday, and everyone makes mistakes, I don't question myself. I don't agonize about past choices, because I trust my self that existed in the past, I trust myself now, and I trust my future self as well. whatever I chose was right at that time, and in that moment. I really, truly believe that divesting yourself from the feelings, opinions and thoughts of others will save your happiness. I still feel incredible empathy for others, because I love all of the good qualities that make a being human, but I simply no longer allow myself to be emotionally or spiritially invested in the vast majority of other people, who are not on the same path of personal development. you can't allow shallow, hideous people to control you. just notice them, and quietly move on. I can't tell you how to achieve this type of self confidence and emotional discipline, but I can say that quiet meditation on who you are does help. the first step is truly accepting yourself, even the ugliest parts. you don't ever have to tell anyone, but you have to accept it and look that hideous thing that happened to you in the eye, and push it aside. you can see it, and acknowledge it, without letting it consume or define you. you're more than the sum of your parts, you know. I just think honest self -reflection, without self blame, as an impartial observer during quiet times, and learning to believe in yourself by challenging yourself and overcoming those challenges is a really great first step. set aside time for yourself to learn about you. think about things like, "why do I feel this way? why did I react that way? what does happiness mean to me? what exactly is upsetting me? why does that upset me? what do I want in my life? what do I believe in?" and so on. get rid of toxic social media, or don't pour over them - just the bare minimum engagement to do your job. focus on yourself, and direct your focus away from other people. that's honestly the best advice that I can give. hearing you cry breaks my heart, because I've been in a similar place, feeling like a stranger amongst a tight knit family every day, or worse, feeling like an old, wizened soul in a room full of shallow toddlers who control your life and happiness. you have to realize that you don't need anyone to understand you to be happy. you don't need anyone to acknowledge you. if you acknowledge yourself from the bottom of your heart, if you know yourself better than anyone else and you've honestly gotten to know the best and worst parts of yourself, you'll gain confidence, and that confidence will shine through in your daily life. people always remember me in a good way, everywhere I go these days, because I'm unusual, so I tend to stand out. my cousin told me that there's something different about me. that I'm intimidating, but empathetic. that I shine in a room full of people. I honestly think it's because I think deeply about myself, and life, and the universe, because I'm not focused on social media, other people, or anything surface level. I always say that most people never think about anything that isn't right in front of their nose. for people like us, who long to think deeply and develop spiritually, learning to think about the things that can't be seen or explained is a great path to happiness. there's a depth of character that a person can develop by looking at yourself honestly, and by looking at the world as an impartial observer, from 1000 feet above. I don't know if any of this advice ((?) if that's what this is, lol), will ever reach you, or if it does reach you, if it will help you, but either way, I really wish you the best. you're extremely beautiful, and you have the capacity emotionally and spiritually to go deeper than most people, which I believe is part of the reason that you feel so empty. focusing on the world, and the shallowest aspects of humanity will lead an old soul to despair, but developing the self and allowing space and time for higher thought will lead an old soul to happiness. good luck with everything Morgan.

I have some advice that honestly has helped me learn to love myself.. when I never did before. Something that really helped me when I used to feel really numb is practicing gratitude. I would write 10 things I am grateful for each morning in detail for 28 days (takes 24 days to form a new habit). It's hard to do it when you are in that state but if you push through, it will change your life for the better. I didn't feel numb after the 28 days were over! I also started recently doing Qigong 10 minutes every day , it's a gentle form of martial arts (kind of like Tai Chi) it's amazing for moving stagnant energy, helps with depression and sleep! Think Vitality with Jeffery Chand is a great youtube channel for learning Qigong!
Something that has helped me post moving cross country and leaving my entire life and having no friends was figuring out my love language and doing things that fulfill that for me. My top love language was acts of service so self care, cleaning, organizing,  yoga and baking/cooking are things that help me feel better. My other love language is quality time, so forcing my self to date myself and go on picnics alone, hikes, reading even though i'm not a reader lolololol I'm liking the book "what I was doing while you were breeding" by Kristin newman.

Take it from a 58yr old mum of three grown sons, depression/anxiety rarely has a defined reason. I suffered with postnatal depression so severe I was hospitalised (not the medical kind either) and I learnt so much from looking back, mainly that some days it felt like my world was caving in and some days 'the sun was shining' but nothing happened to make those days different! My husband has often talked about coming in from work not knowing what version of me would be there, sunshine happy or sobbing because I forgot to buy eggs that day...I noticed you trying to convince yourself that everything would be ok or smiling when you really wanted to cry, pretending to 'enjoy' yourself because you don't want others to worry about you . I saw myself in your eyes, worried what people will think if you fall apart. Teach yourself to be aware that it's ok to have bad days when you're dealing with depression, it doesn't mean you're not getting better, it just means that today is a tough day. Keep a mini journal of good days (or hours) and bad days, over the course of a month try to aim for more good days than bad. You may have already done this but just in case, get your thyroid levels checked (I didn't get diagnosed till I was almost 40!) and your Vitamin B/hormone levels checked. So many people think vitamins aren't important because you can buy them over the counter, but the B vitamins (there's a few) are massively important to your mind and body, I only know this because my thyroid condition means I can't store them no matter how healthy I eat. If I sound like a fruit loop, ask google lol...and please, just don't rule out a medical reason for your anxiety/depression. Sorry for the ramble but I wish someone had told me in my 20's what I know now. xx

Girl, I HIGHLY recommend the book "The Art of Extreme Self Care" by Cheryl Richarson. It's a pretty short read but sooooo amazing. It shows us all the ways we are depriving ourselves, how our boundaries with others can affect us mentally, how extreme self care is the key to enhancing our energy, productivity, motivation, and inspiration, and how saying NO to others is a full sentence. We don't need to explain ourselves. We don't need to constantly give to others. We deserve to put ourselves first. We often deprive ourselves in more ways than we can count. I cried reading that book because it rang so true for me. And I also recommend it to my clients (even though I'm a lucid dream coach, it is helpful for EVERYONE to read this book). Our bodies will always be the first to tell us when something is wrong, and we just need to listen to those signals. I don't believe emotions come up for no reason. You're on your way to expanding into something greater which is why your current environment doesn't feel like it fits you anymore, you're energetically preparing for so much more. I hope that this book serves you and I hope that you honor your own needs and desires before other's. You deserve it.

Morgan, i'm a 25 year old law student from the Netherlands that is very blessed, and also depressed. I am 'figuring it out' as well and im in a  better place right now, than I was a year ago. It comes and it goes like the weather. There's always these trigger moments (like your soul cycle class) and we have to be aware of them and how they can slowly push us into that irrational and dark well. This might sounds cringy, but what worked for me (besides the psychologist, and the anti-depressants, God) is slowly coming to this strong realisation that I deserve to love myself. That we are not born, we are not destined to be on this planet just to feel unloved and unhappy. It's futile. Be a giant, let the world be small. And don't expect others to treat you, like the way you would treat them. Unfortunately, that's just not the way this world works. But continue treating them, like the way you want to be treated. And I think, that as you're evolving (btw, that 'not a breakdown, but a break though' shows your wisdom) the universe will put the right people on your path. So, thank you. It's brave but very important to share depression. Those thoughts of low self esteem, having 'no future' and 'grieving' a past life you're describing are familiar to me. But please remember that it is the irrational depression talking. I don't want to be preachy, but if I can at least help someone with my comment it is worth my energy. Cherish every happy moment, hold on to your inner circle of people that love you unconditionally; try and love yourself unconditionally as well and never lose hope.

What can happen when you have past trauma is that when you are exposed to toxic experiences like this your brain reads it as danger! This is to protect you as it has done for many years!! What then can happen is that afterward your brain will have brain fog... as it is trying to navigate through the following days. Brain fog is very real!! And can make you feel like you are loosing your mind at times. I speak from experience.  You are NOT crazy! During times of brain fog you can't focus, it is difficult to find words or to complete any so called simple task. You will also find you are tired. Like exhausted!  Your brain flooding your body with cortisol which in small doses helps us in those fight, flight or freeze times. When you are being constantly flooded with it you have overwhelming feelings or your brain will numb you out. But once you start to come out of the fog it can be insanely confusing and we overthinking the fuck out of it! And blaming ourselves is often what happens! When it is not your fault at all!! Talk therapy can help you make sense of what is happening. Be gentle and kind with yourself!
